grading and backfilling operations during mass grading for the Aulani, A Disney Resort & Spa
project (formerly Disney’s Grand Hawaiian Resort & Spa) from February 4, 2009 through
April 2, 2010. The results of our field observations and tests are provided in the enclosed mass
grading observation and testing report for the project dated May 20, 2010.
| certify that Geolabs performed the earthwork compaction tests. To the best of our
knowledge, it is our professional opinion that the grading and backfilling work (Item No. 13 of the
Special Inspection form) for the project observed and tested by Geolabs have been constructed in
general conformance with the intent of the approved plans and specifications and our
geotechnical engineering report and subsequent recommendations provided for the above
project.

Subject: Mass Grading Observation and Testing Report
Aulani
A Disney Resort & Spa
Ko Olina, Oahu, Hawaii
Reference: Report by Geolabs, Inc. dated September 30, 2008
entitled "Geotechnical Engineering Exploration,
Disney's Grand Hawaiian Resort & Spa
Ko Olina, Oahu, Hawaii”
Grading Permit No.: GP2009-11-0642
Dear Mr. Rochat:
As requested, we provided geotechnical engineering services during the mass
grading of Aulani, A Disney Resort & Spa in the Ko Olina area of the Island of Oahu,
Hawaii. This letter report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observation and
consultation services performed for the mass grading portion of the project only. The
discussions presented herein are subject to the limitations noted at the end of this letter
report.
Project Considerations
Aulani, A Disney Resort & Spa (formerly Disney’s Grand Hawaiian Resort & Spa)
project site is within the existing Ko Olina Resort development in the District of Ewa on the
Island of Oahu, Hawaii (as shown on the Project Location Map, Plate 1). The project site
encompasses two parcels of land (Lot Nos. 13 and 15) fronting Lagoon No. 1 of the
Ko Olina Resort. The project site is also adjacent to the existing JW Marriott Ihilani Resort
and Spa (to the northwest). The two parcels are to the southwest of Ali inui Drive, which is
the main entry road into the resort. A General Site Plan is provided on Plate 2.
Our observation and testing services during the mass grading of the project
occurred between February 4, 2009 and April 2, 2010. Hawaiian Dredging Construction
Company was the general contractor for the project, and Jayar Construction was the site
work subcontractor for the project.
2006 Kalihi Street * Honolulu, Hawaii 96819
Phone: (808) 841-5064 * Facsimile: (808) 847-1749 »* E-mail: hawaii@qgeolabs.net
Hawaii * California

W.O. 5872-30 (Aulani, A Disney Resort & Spa) (Grading Permit No. GP2009-11-0642)
May 20, 2010
Discussion and Recommendations
Earthwork at the Aulani site generally consisted of cuts and fills of less than about
5 feet except for some areas where the cuts and fills extended up to 15 to 25 feet thick. A
site plan of the project is provided on Plate 2.
Fill and backfill materials generally consisted of excavated materials from the
Aulani project site and some imported materials. In general, fill materials consisted of
materials less than 3 inches in maximum particle size. Samples of the on-site and
imported materials were obtained and transported to our office for testing, where
appropriate. The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were
established in our laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D 1557 (Modified
Proctor), and the test results are summarized on Plate 3.
The fill and backfill materials generally were moisture-conditioned to above
optimum moisture content, placed in loose lifts, and compacted to a minimum of
90 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in accordance with ASTM D 1557.
The compaction requirement generally was increased to a minimum of 95 percent of the
maximum dry density for the last lift of fills under pavements (finished pavement
subgrades).
Subgrades in the cut areas generally were scarified and recompacted to obtain a
minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density as determined in accordance with
ASTM D 1557.
During the earthwork operations, periodic field density tests were performed in
general accordance with ASTM D 6938 (Nuclear Gauge Method), where appropriate. The
compaction test results are summarized on Plates 4.1 through 4.172 presented herein.
These tests were performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed fills and
backfills at the site. Test locations and elevations were estimated by pacing and
interpolating from on-site survey stakes, where available. These locations and elevations
should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used. Areas
assessed to be unsatisfactory generally were reworked until the specified minimum
compaction was obtained and/or accepted by our field representative based on visual
observation and hand probing.
Due to placement of fills of up to about 25 feet in height, a settlement monitoring
program was implemented during the mass grading operations. Twenty-eight settlement
gauges were installed, as shown on the Site Plan, Plate 2. The purpose of the settlement
monitoring program was to monitor the magnitude and rates of ground settlement due to
the placement of new fills on site. The ground settlements were monitored for a period
ranging from about 12 to 25 weeks. Based on the settlement gauge readings, ground
settlements of up to about 2.2 inches were observed at the site. Based on the settlement
gauge readings, it appeared that the elevation readings of the gauges indicate that the
settlements generally have stabilized under the new fill loads. It should be noted that
residual settlements (post construction settlements) on the order of about 1 inch still may
occur over a long period following completion of construction.
GEOLABS, INC.
Hawaii e California
Walt Disney Imagineering Page 3
W.O. 5872-30 (Aulani, A Disney Resort & Spa) (Grading Permit No. GP2009- 11-0642)
May 20, 2010
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the referenced tests, it
is our professional opinion that the mass grading operations for the Aulani site observed
by Geolabs in the period covered in this report were performed in general conformance
with the intent of the project plans and specifications and the geotechnical
recommendations presented in the referenced report and subsequent recommendations
and amendments.
It should be noted the above statement of professional opinion is based on the
grades existing at the completion of the mass grading operations of the project in
April 2010. Geolabs assumes no responsibility for any alterations made to the slopes or
finished grades on the above project subsequent to our observation and testing period
without our knowledge and written acknowledgment.
Limitations
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Therefore, some of the earthwork may
have been performed without our observation. However, the level of earthwork
observation and testing services provided appears to be reasonable in reducing some of
the geotechnical risks to the project.
It should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and statistical
repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor the earthwork construction and
materials. Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards
of geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee
construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of
when they are found.
